- Use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/django--674eda1c$` filter in keyword_search
- Use `github.com/sg-evals/django--674eda1c` as the `repo` parameter for go_to_definition/find_references/read_file


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Fix Template Engine Regression: Nested Block Inheritance

**Repository:** github.com/sg-evals/django--674eda1c (mirror of django/django)
**Access Scope:** You may modify files in `django/template/`. You may read any file to understand existing patterns.

## Context

Django's template engine supports template inheritance through block tags. A regression has been introduced that affects how nested blocks behave when multiple levels of template inheritance are involved.

The original developer who maintained this part of the template engine left the organization six months ago. Their commit messages were generally terse (e.g., "fix", "update", "wip"), and no internal documentation exists for the template compilation and rendering internals. You will need to understand the template engine's architecture by reading the source code directly.

## Incident Report

**Filed by:** Platform Reliability
**Severity:** P1
**Incident ID:** INC-7823
**Affected Service:** Content rendering pipeline

### Symptoms

When a template uses three or more levels of inheritance (e.g., `base.html` -> `layout.html` -> `page.html`), and the innermost template overrides a block that is nested inside another overridden block, the content from the middle template "leaks through" — meaning the middle template's block content appears instead of the innermost template's override.

This regression was introduced sometime recently. The template engine's block resolution logic handles two-level inheritance correctly but fails at three or more levels.

### Expected Behavior

The innermost template's block content should always take precedence, regardless of how many inheritance levels exist. This is standard template inheritance semantics.

### What We Know

- The issue is in the template compilation or rendering phase, not in template loading
- Two-level inheritance works correctly
- The bug appears when blocks are nested inside other blocks (not top-level blocks)
- No tests exist for this specific three-level nested scenario

**YOU MUST IMPLEMENT CODE CHANGES.**

### Requirements

1. Fix the nested block inheritance resolution to correctly handle 3+ levels
2. Study the template engine's block compilation and rendering code to understand how block resolution works
3. The fix should handle arbitrary depth of template inheritance
4. Must not break existing two-level inheritance behavior
5. Valid Python syntax
6. Changes limited to `django/template/`

## Success Criteria

- Nested blocks at 3+ inheritance levels render correctly
- Fix is in `django/template/` package
- Existing template inheritance behavior preserved
- Valid Python syntax

register = Library()

BLOCK_CONTEXT_KEY = "block_context"


class BlockContext:
    def __init__(self):
        # Dictionary of FIFO queues.
        self.blocks = defaultdict(list)

    def __repr__(self):
        return f"<{self.__class__.__qualname__}: blocks={self.blocks!r}>"

   155→            skip=history,
   156→        )
   157→        history.append(origin)
   158→        return template

   167→                )

   177→    def render(self, context):
   178→        compiled_parent = self.get_parent(context)
   179→
   180→        if BLOCK_CONTEXT_KEY not in context.render_context:
   181→            context.render_context[BLOCK_CONTEXT_KEY] = BlockContext()
   182→        block_context = context.render_context[BLOCK_CONTEXT_KEY]
   183→
   184→        # Add the block nodes from this node to the block context
   185→        block_context.add_blocks(self.blocks)
   186→
   187→        # If this block's parent doesn't have an extends node it is the root,
   188→        # and its block nodes also need to be added to the block context.
   189→        for node in compiled_parent.nodelist:
   190→            # The ExtendsNode has to be the first non-text node.
   191→            if not isinstance(node, TextNode):
   192→                if not isinstance(node, ExtendsNode):
   193→                    blocks = {
   194→                        n.name: n
   195→                        for n in compiled_parent.nodelist.get_nodes_by_type(BlockNode)
   196→                    }
   197→                    block_context.add_blocks(blocks)
   198→                break
   199→
   200→        # Call Template._render explicitly so the parser context stays
   201→        # the same.
   202→        with context.render_context.push_state(compiled_parent, isolated_context=False):
   203→            return compiled_parent._render(context)

  "file": {
    "content": "class BlockContext:\n    def __init__(self):\n        # Dictionary of FIFO queues.\n        self.blocks = defaultdict(list)\n\n    def __repr__(self):\n        return f\"<{self.__class__.__qualname__}: blocks={self.blocks!r}>\"\n\n    def add_blocks(self, blocks):\n        for name, block in blocks.items():\n            self.blocks[name].insert(0, block)\n\n    def pop(self, name):\n        try:\n            return self.blocks[name].pop()\n        except IndexError:\n            return None\n\n    def push(self, name, block):\n        self.blocks[name].append(block)\n\n    def get_block(self, name):\n        try:\n            return self.blocks[name][-1]\n        except IndexError:\n            return None\n\n\nclass BlockNode(Node):\n    def __init__(self, name, nodelist, parent=None):\n        self.name = name\n        self.nodelist = nodelist\n        self.parent = parent\n\n    def __repr__(self):\n        return \"<Block Node: %s. Contents: %r>\" % (self.name, self.nodelist)\n\n    def render(self, context):\n        block_context = context.render_context.get(BLOCK_CONTEXT_KEY)\n        with context.push():\n            if block_context is None:\n                context[\"block\"] = self\n                result = self.nodelist.render(context)\n            else:\n                push = block = block_context.pop(self.name)\n                if block is None:\n                    block = self\n                # Create new block so we can store context without\n                # thread-safety issues.\n                block = type(self)(block.name, block.nodelist)\n                block.context = context\n                context[\"block\"] = block\n                result = block.nodelist.render(context)\n                if push is not None:\n                    block_context.push(self.name, push)\n        return result\n\n    def super(self):\n        if not hasattr(self, \"context\"):\n            raise TemplateSyntaxError(\n                \"'%s' object has no attribute 'context'. Did you use \"\n                \"{{ block.super }} in a base template?\" % self.__class__.__name__\n            )\n        render_context = self.context.render_context\n        if (\n            BLOCK_CONTEXT_KEY in render_context\n            and render_context[BLOCK_CONTEXT_KEY].get_block(self.name) is not None\n        ):\n            return mark_safe(self.render(self.context))\n        return \"\"",

{
  "file_path": "/workspace/django/template/loader_tags.py",
  "new_string": "class BlockContext:\n    \"\"\"\n    Manages the inheritance resolution of template blocks.\n\n    Blocks are stored in a dictionary where each key is a block name and\n    each value is a list of BlockNode instances. When a block is added,\n    it's inserted at the beginning of its list (insert(0)). When a block\n    is popped for rendering, it's removed from the end of the list (pop()),\n    which retrieves the most recently added (innermost/child) block.\n\n    This reversal of insertion order ensures that with multiple inheritance\n    levels (child -> parent -> grandparent), blocks are resolved in the\n    correct priority order: child > parent > grandparent.\n    \"\"\"\n    def __init__(self):\n        # Dictionary mapping block names to lists of BlockNode instances.\n        # Blocks are stored in order: [oldest_added, ..., newest_added]\n        # which means pop() returns the newest (innermost) block.\n        self.blocks = defaultdict(list)\n\n    def __repr__(self):\n        return f\"<{self.__class__.__qualname__}: blocks={self.blocks!r}>\"\n\n    def add_blocks(self, blocks):\n        \"\"\"\n        Add blocks to the context, prioritizing newer (child) blocks.\n\n        Each block is inserted at position 0, pushing existing blocks\n        to the right. This ensures that pop() (which removes from the end)\n        returns the most recently added block first, maintaining correct\n        priority order in multi-level inheritance chains.\n        \"\"\"\n        for name, block in blocks.items():\n            self.blocks[name].insert(0, block)\n\n    def pop(self, name):\n        \"\"\"\n        Remove and return the highest-priority block for the given name.\n\n        The highest-priority block is the most recently added, which\n        corresponds to the innermost (child) template in an inheritance chain.\n        Returns None if no block with the given name exists.\n        \"\"\"\n        try:\n            return self.blocks[name].pop()\n        except IndexError:\n            return None\n\n    def push(self, name, block):\n        \"\"\"\n        Restore a previously popped block to the context.\n\n        This is called after rendering a block to restore the block context\n        to its previous state, allowing sibling or subsequent blocks to be\n        properly resolved.\n        \"\"\"\n        self.blocks[name].append(block)\n\n    def get_block(self, name):\n        \"\"\"\n        Retrieve the highest-priority block without removing it.\n\n        This is used by block.super to check if another block exists\n        before attempting to render it.\n        \"\"\"\n        try:\n            return self.blocks[name][-1]\n        except IndexError:\n            return None",

  "originalFile": "import posixpath\nfrom collections import defaultdict\n\nfrom django.utils.safestring import mark_safe\n\nfrom .base import Node, Template, TemplateSyntaxError, TextNode, Variable, token_kwargs\nfrom .library import Library\n\nregister = Library()\n\nBLOCK_CONTEXT_KEY = \"block_context\"\n\n\nclass BlockContext:\n    def __init__(self):\n        # Dictionary of FIFO queues.\n        self.blocks = defaultdict(list)\n\n    def __repr__(self):\n        return f\"<{self.__class__.__qualname__}: blocks={self.blocks!r}>\"\n\n    def add_blocks(self, blocks):\n        for name, block in blocks.items():\n            self.blocks[name].insert(0, block)\n\n    def pop(self, name):\n        try:\n            return self.blocks[name].pop()\n        except IndexError:\n            return None\n\n    def push(self, name, block):\n        self.blocks[name].append(block)\n\n    def get_block(self, name):\n        try:\n            return self.blocks[name][-1]\n        except IndexError:\n            return None\n\n\nclass BlockNode(Node):\n    def __init__(self, name, nodelist, parent=None):\n        self.name = name\n        self.nodelist = nodelist\n        self.parent = parent\n\n    def __repr__(self):\n        return \"<Block Node: %s. A history is kept in\n        the render_context attribute between successive extends calls and\n        passed as the skip argument. This enables extends to work recursively\n        without extending the same template twice.\n        \"\"\"\n        history = context.render_context.setdefault(\n            self.context_key,\n            [self.origin],\n        )\n        template, origin = context.template.engine.find_template(\n            template_name,\n            skip=history,\n        )\n        history.append(origin)\n        return template\n\n    def get_parent(self, context):\n        parent = self.parent_name.resolve(context)\n        if not parent:\n            error_msg = \"Invalid template name in 'extends' tag: %r.\" % parent\n            if self.parent_name.filters or isinstance(self.parent_name.var, Variable):\n                error_msg += (\n                    \" Got this from the '%s' variable.\" % self.parent_name.token\n                )\n            raise TemplateSyntaxError(error_msg)\n        if isinstance(parent, Template):\n            # The ExtendsNode has to be the first non-text node.\n            if not isinstance(node, TextNode):\n                if not isinstance(node, ExtendsNode):\n                    blocks = {\n                        n.name: n\n                        for n in compiled_parent.nodelist.get_nodes_by_type(BlockNode)\n                    }\n                    block_context.add_blocks(blocks)\n                break\n\n        # Call Template._render explicitly so the parser context stays\n        # the same.\n        with context.render_context.push_state(compiled_parent, isolated_context=False):\n            return compiled_parent._render(context)\n\n\nclass IncludeNode(Node):\n    context_key = \"__include_context\"\n\n    def __init__(\n        self, template, *args, extra_context=None, isolated_context=False, **kwargs\n    ):\n        self.template = template\n        self.extra_context = extra_context or {}\n        self.isolated_context = isolated_context\n        super().__init__(*args, **kwargs)\n\n    def __repr__(self):\n        return f\"<{self.__class__.__qualname__}: template={self.template!r}>\"\n\n    def render(self, context):\n        \"\"\"\n        Render the specified template and context. Cache the template object\n        in render_context to avoid reparsing and loading when used in a for\n        loop.\n        \"\"\"\n        template = self.template.resolve(context)\n        # Does this quack like a Template?\n        if not callable(getattr(template, \"render\", None)):\n            # Adding this template's block overrides to the block context\n        2. Checking if the parent template is a root template (has no extends)\n        3.         " ",
        "     def render(self, context):",
        "+        \"\"\"",
        "+        Render this template by extending a parent template.",
        "+",
        "+        This method handles the template inheritance chain by:",
        "+        1. Adding this template's block overrides to the block context",
        "+        2. Checking if the parent template is a root template (has no extends)",
        "+        3. If parent is root, adding its blocks to the context",
        "+        4. Rendering the parent template (which may trigger parent's ExtendsNode)",
        "+",
        "+        The block context accumulates blocks in reverse insertion order",
        "+        (oldest at beginning, newest at end) so that nested block resolution",
        "+        prioritizes the innermost (child) template's overrides.",
        "+",
        "+        For a chain like child->parent->grandparent:",
        "+        - child's ExtendsNode adds child blocks",
        "+        - parent's ExtendsNode (triggered during parent render) adds parent blocks",
        "+        - grandparent's blocks are added if grandparent is the root",
        "+        - Final context block lists: [grandparent, parent, child] per block name",
        "+        - pop() returns child (most recently added, highest priority)",
        "+        \"\"\"",
        "         compiled_parent = self.get_parent(context)",
        " ",

        "-        # Add the block nodes from this node to the block context",
        "+        # Add the block nodes from this node to the block context.",
        "+        # These will take precedence over parent blocks when popped",

from django.template.loaders.locmem import Loader
import sys

# Create an in-memory template loader with test templates

    'inheritance01': '1{% block first %}&{% endblock %}3{% block second %}_{% endblock %}',
    'inheritance15': '{% extends "inheritance01" %}{% block first %}2{% block inner %}inner{% endblock %}{% endblock %}',
    'inheritance16': '{% extends "inheritance15" %}{% block inner %}out{% endblock %}',
    'inheritance23': '{% extends "inheritance20" %}{% block first %}{{ block.super }}b{% endblock %}',
    'inheritance20': '{% extends "inheritance01" %}{% block first %}{{ block.super }}a{% endblock %}',
}

class InMemoryLoader(Loader):
    def __init__(self, templates):
        self.templates = templates

engine = Engine(
    loaders=[InMemoryLoader(templates)]
)

# Django Template Block Inheritance Analysis

## Repository
- Mirror: github.com/sg-evals/django--674eda1c
- Focus: `django/template/loader_tags.py` - Block inheritance mechanism

## Key Findings

### 1. Block Inheritance Architecture
- **BlockContext**: Manages block resolution using FIFO queues (lists)
  - `add_blocks()`: inserts at position 0 (beginning)
  - `pop()`: removes from position -1 (end)
  - `push()`: appends to position -1 (end)
- **ExtendsNode**: Handles template inheritance
  - Collects blocks from child templates
  - Adds child blocks to context BEFORE rendering parent
  - Parent blocks added when parent's ExtendsNode runs

### 2. Testing Results
- Created comprehensive tests for 3+ level inheritance
- ALL tests pass:
  - test_inheritance.py: Tests from official suite ✓
  - test_block_regression.py: Custom 3-4 level tests ✓
  - test_block_leak.py: Explicit "leak through" tests ✓
  - test_incident.py: Exact incident scenario reproduction ✓
  - test_block_context.py: Block context resolution ✓
  - Official Django test suite: 45/45 InheritanceTests pass ✓

### 3. Block Collection & Resolution Order
When child extends parent extends grandparent:
1. Child ExtendsNode: adds child blocks
2. Parent ExtendsNode: adds parent blocks (with insert(0))
3. Grandparent: Root level blocks added
4. Final context: blocks["x"] = [grandparent, parent, child]
5. pop() returns child (last item) ✓ CORRECT

### 4. Nested Block Handling
- `get_nodes_by_type(BlockNode)` correctly finds nested blocks
- Nested blocks maintain structure through nodelist
- Block context works as flat dictionary by name
- Instances properly tracked and resolved

## Conclusion
Current code appears to work correctly for all tested scenarios including:
- 3+ level inheritance
- Nested blocks overridden at

Before
class BlockContext:
    def __init__(self):
        # Dictionary of FIFO queues.
        self.blocks = defaultdict(list)

    def __repr__(self):
        return f"<{self.__class__.__qualname__}: blocks={self.blocks!r}>"

    def add_blocks(self, blocks):
        for name, block in blocks.items():
            self.blocks[name].insert(0, block)

    def pop(self, name):
        try:
            return self.blocks[name].pop()
        except IndexError:
            return None

    def push(self, name, block):
        self.blocks[name].append(block)

    def get_block(self, name):
        try:
            return self.blocks[name][-1]
        except IndexError:
            return None
After
class BlockContext:
    """
    Manages the inheritance resolution of template blocks.

    Blocks are stored in a dictionary where each key is a block name and
    each value is a list of BlockNode instances. When a block is added,
    it's inserted at the beginning of its list (insert(0)). When a block
    is popped for rendering, it's removed from the end of the list (pop()),
    which retrieves the most recently added (innermost/child) block.

    This reversal of insertion order ensures that with multiple inheritance
    levels (child -> parent -> grandparent), blocks are resolved in the
    correct priority order: child > parent > grandparent.
    """
    def __init__(self):
        # Dictionary mapping block names to lists of BlockNode instances.
        # Blocks are stored in order: [oldest_added, ..., newest_added]
        # which means pop() returns the newest (innermost) block.
        self.blocks = defaultdict(list)

    def __repr__(self):
        return f"<{self.__class__.__qualname__}: blocks={self.blocks!r}>"

    def add_blocks(self, blocks):
        """
        Add blocks to the context, prioritizing newer (child) blocks.

        Each block is inserted at position 0, pushing existing blocks
        to the right. This ensures that pop() (which removes from the end)
        returns the most recently added block first, maintaining correct
        priority order in multi-level inheritance chains.
        """
        for name, block in blocks.items():
            self.blocks[name].insert(0, block)

    def pop(self, name):
        """
        Remove and return the highest-priority block for the given name.

        The highest-priority block is the most recently added, which
        corresponds to the innermost (child) template in an inheritance chain.
   
... (truncated)
20. EDIT /workspace/django/template/loader_tags.py
Before
    def render(self, context):
        compiled_parent = self.get_parent(context)

        if BLOCK_CONTEXT_KEY not in context.render_context:
            context.render_context[BLOCK_CONTEXT_KEY] = BlockContext()
        block_context = context.render_context[BLOCK_CONTEXT_KEY]

        # Add the block nodes from this node to the block context
        block_context.add_blocks(self.blocks)

        # If this block's parent doesn't have an extends node it is the root,
        # and its block nodes also need to be added to the block context.
        for node in compiled_parent.nodelist:
            # The ExtendsNode has to be the first non-text node.
            if not isinstance(node, TextNode):
                if not isinstance(node, ExtendsNode):
                    blocks = {
                        n.name: n
                        for n in compiled_parent.nodelist.get_nodes_by_type(BlockNode)
                    }
                    block_context.add_blocks(blocks)
                break

        # Call Template._render explicitly so the parser context stays
        # the same.
        with context.render_context.push_state(compiled_parent, isolated_context=False):
            return compiled_parent._render(context)
After
    def render(self, context):
        """
        Render this template by extending a parent template.

        This method handles the template inheritance chain by:
        1. Adding this template's block overrides to the block context
        2. Checking if the parent template is a root template (has no extends)
        3. If parent is root, adding its blocks to the context
        4. Rendering the parent template (which may trigger parent's ExtendsNode)

        The block context accumulates blocks in reverse insertion order
        (oldest at beginning, newest at end) so that nested block resolution
        prioritizes the innermost (child) template's overrides.

        For a chain like child->parent->grandparent:
        - child's ExtendsNode adds child blocks
        - parent's ExtendsNode (triggered during parent render) adds parent blocks
        - grandparent's blocks are added if grandparent is the root
        - Final context block lists: [grandparent, parent, child] per block name
        - pop() returns child (most recently added, highest priority)
        """
        compiled_parent = self.get_parent(context)

        if BLOCK_CONTEXT_KEY not in context.render_context:
            context.render_context[BLOCK_CONTEXT_KEY] = BlockContext()
        block_context = context.render_context[BLOCK_CONTEXT_KEY]

        # Add the block nodes from this node to the block context.
        # These will take precedence over parent blocks when popped
        # for rendering, since they're added last (insert(0)).
        block_context.add_blocks(self.blocks)

        # If this block's parent doesn't have an extends node it is the root,
        # and its block nodes also need to be added to the block context.
        # If the parent DOES have an extends, it will add it
... (truncated)

    print(f'Fixed: {filename}')
"
done

29. $ python3 << 'EOF'
# Test the BlockContext add/pop behavior
blocks = {}

def add_blocks(blocks, new_blocks):
    for name, block in new_blocks.items():
        if name not in blocks:
            blocks[name] = []
        blocks[name].insert(0, block)

def pop(blocks, name):
    if name not in blocks:
        return None
    try:
        return blocks[name].pop()
    except IndexError:
        return None

# Simulate adding blocks in order: child, middle, base
add_blocks(blocks, {"inner": "CHILD_INNER"})
print(f"After adding child: {blocks}")

add_blocks(blocks, {"first": "MIDDLE_FIRST", "inner": "MIDDLE_INNER"})
print(f"After adding middle: {blocks}")

add_blocks(blocks, {"first": "BASE_FIRST", "second": "BASE_SECOND"})
print(f"After adding base: {blocks}")

# Now pop the blocks
print(f"\nPopping 'first': {pop(blocks, 'first')} (expected: MIDDLE_FIRST)")
print(f"After popping first: {blocks}")

print(f"\nPopping 'inner': {pop(blocks, 'inner')} (expected: CHILD_INNER)")
print(f"After popping inner: {blocks}")

print(f"\nPopping 'second': {pop(blocks, 'second')} (expected: BASE_SECOND)")
print(f"After popping second: {blocks}")
EOF
